Apply all modifiers before rolling.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e+X Modifier\u003c/b\u003e: Makes the roll easier, reducing the Target Number by X.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e-X Modifier:\u003c/b\u003e Makes the roll harder, increasing the Target Number by X.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eModifiers from different named sources are cumulative unless otherwise stated.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eEXAMPLE:\u003c/b\u003e A Marine needs \u003cb\u003e5+\u003c/b\u003e to hit.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003e+1 Modifier\u003c/b\u003e reduces the Target Number by 1. He now hits on \u003cb\u003e4+\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003e-1 Modifier\u003c/b\u003e increases the Target Number by 1. He now hits on \u003cb\u003e6+\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eAbility text: \"+1 to Armour\" means the \u003cb\u003eArmour Roll\u003c/b\u003e improves (Target Number decreases). \"-1 to Hit\" means hitting becomes harder (Target Number increases).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA Target Number can never be modified below 2+ or above 6+.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE:\u003c/b\u003e Modifiers adjust the Target Number, not the dice roll itself. This keeps arithmetic simple, as a player always knows exactly what the Target Number is before rolling the dice. It also ensures that automatic successes on a roll of 6 and automatic failures on a roll of 1 are clear, no matter how many modifiers are applied to a single roll."

Every Test follows the same logic: there is a Target Number, the player rolls, and the result either meets the threshold or it does not.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eTests come in two flavours:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eCharacteristic Tests \u003c/b\u003euse a value from the Unit’s own profile, its Armour, its Evade, and its native resilience. When a squad of Marines takes fire and rolls their \u003cb\u003eArmour Rolls\u003c/b\u003e, that is a Characteristic Test.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eAttribute Tests \u003c/b\u003euse a value from a Weapon Profile or Special Rule, such as a weapon’s Hit characteristic. When those same Marines fire their C-14 Rifles and roll to hit, that is an Attribute Test.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eNot everything involving dice is a Test. \u003cb\u003eValue Generation\u003c/b\u003e - a \u003cb\u003eCharge Roll\u003c/b\u003e, a D3 \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eresult, simply produces a number. The player adds the die result to the base value as instructed. There is no Target Number to beat.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eTo resolve any Test: identify the base Target Number, apply all Modifiers to determine the final Target Number, and roll the die. If the result is equal to or exceeds the Target Number, the Test succeeds. If it falls short, the Test fails."

                                  "stringValue": "Every shot, every ability, and every order that requires a clear view of the target follows the same process. \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e determines what a model can see and, by extension, what it can shoot at.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003ci\u003eStarCraft: The Miniatures Game\u003c/i\u003e uses a \u003cb\u003e2D Line of Sight (LoS)\u003c/b\u003e system. All \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight \u003c/b\u003echecks are resolved from a top-down perspective, looking directly down at the battlefield from above.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eTo determine whether an acting model can see a target, trace an imaginary straight line from \u003cb\u003eany part\u003c/b\u003e of the acting model’s base to \u003cb\u003eany part\u003c/b\u003e of the target model’s base.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf the line does not pass through any \u003cb\u003eBlocking Terrain\u003c/b\u003e (any terrain piece with an \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of 1 or greater - see Part 11), the target is Visible. No further checks are required.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf the line passes through \u003cb\u003eBlocking Terrain\u003c/b\u003e, the target is not automatically hidden. Check the \u003cb\u003eCover\u003c/b\u003e rules (Part 7.1.1) to determine whether the terrain actually blocks \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e. Terrain that intersects the trace but does not meet the requirements for \u003cb\u003eFull Cover\u003c/b\u003e or \u003cb\u003eDirect Cover\u003c/b\u003e does not block \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e. The target remains Visible.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eFor \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e purposes, a terrain piece’s footprint is defined by its physical base or, if it has no base, the outermost edges of its solid structure viewed from above. Unless players agree otherwise during Battlefield Setup, gaps, windows, doorways, and open interiors within the footprint \u003cb\u003edo block \u003c/b\u003ethe \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA terrain opening may be passable for movement without counting as open for \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e (see Part 4.6 for Gap Clearance rules).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003ePlayers must agree during Battlefield Setup on the footprint of each terrain piece and on which openings, if any, count as passable gaps for movement.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDesigner’s note: \u003c/b\u003eOur game uses a top-down \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e method rather than a precise measurement from the model’s eye. This prevents disputes over exact posture, slouching torsos, and weapon placement. It also ensures terrain interacts correctly regardless of model posture or base design. The downside is a slight loss of cinematic feel, but it is well worth it for speed and balance."

                                              "stringValue": "Terrain pieces may block the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e between models. A terrain piece provides Cover in one of two ways:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFull Cover:\u003c/b\u003e A terrain piece blocks\u003cb\u003e Line of Sight\u003c/b\u003e if its\u003cb\u003e Effective Size \u003c/b\u003e(Part 7.1.2) is \u003cb\u003eequal \u003c/b\u003eto or \u003cb\u003egreater \u003c/b\u003ethan the \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of \u003cb\u003eboth \u003c/b\u003ethe \u003cb\u003eAttacker \u003c/b\u003eand the Target. Neither model can see over the terrain - \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is blocked.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDirect Cover:\u003c/b\u003e If the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sigh\u003c/b\u003et trace passes through a terrain piece, and either the Attacker or the target is\u003cb\u003e Within 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of that terrain, the Line of Sight between them is blocked, provided the terrain piece's Effective Size is equal to or greater than the Effective Size of the model that is \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eException:\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e If both the Attacker and the target are \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003e1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the same terrain piece and \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003e3\"\u003c/b\u003e of each other, this rule does not apply. Resolve \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e normally using the standard trace (Part 7.1)\u003cb\u003e.\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEach terrain piece is assessed for Cover independently. Terrain pieces do not combine their Effective Size or proximity. If no single terrain piece meets the requirements for Full Cover or Direct Cover, \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight \u003c/b\u003eis not blocked, regardless of how many terrain pieces the trace passes through.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eIn this example, \u003c/b\u003ea player checks \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e from a Goliath (Size 3) to a Unit of five Marines (Size 2) through a ruined wall (Size 2). The wall is too short to block the Goliath’s view entirely - Full Cover fails. However, two Marines are \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003e1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the wall. Because the wall’s Size equals the Marines’ Size, the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e to and from those two Marines is blocked - they are not Visible to the Goliath, and the Goliath is not Visible to them. The remaining three Marines are too far from the wall and are Visible normally.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eElevation Dead Zone\u003c/b\u003e If a model on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e (Size 3+) draws\u003cb\u003e Line of Sight\u003c/b\u003e to a model at \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e that is \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the base of the same terrain piece, \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is blocked. This applies in both directions - neither model can see the other.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eException:\u003c/b\u003e If both models are \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the same terrain piece and \u003cb\u003eWithin 3\"\u003c/b\u003e of each other, this rule does not apply. Resolve \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e normally using the standard trace (Part 7.1).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example:\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e a Marine on \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e checks \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e to a Zergling at \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e. The Zergling is \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eWithin 1\" \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003eof the base of the same terrain piece the Marine is standing on, but the two models are more than 3\" apart. The Zergling is too close to the foot of the cliff to be seen from above - \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e is blocked. This works in both directions - the Zergling cannot see the Marine above it either. If the two models were \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eWithin 3\" \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003eof each other, Close Quarters would apply, and standard \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e rules would be used instead.\u003c/i\u003e"

                                "title": {
                                  "stringValue": "7.1.2 Verticality and Effective Size"
                                },
                                "subSubItems": {
                                  "arrayValue": {}
                                },
                                "content": {
                                  "arrayValue": {
                                    "values": [
                                      {
                                        "mapValue": {
                                          "fields": {
                                            "type": {
                                              "stringValue": "text"
                                            },
                                            "value": {
                                              "stringValue": "When a model stands on top of a terrain piece (such as \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e):\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eEffective Size \u003c/b\u003eis equal to the model Size plus the terrain Size.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eEXAMPLE:\u003c/b\u003e A Marine (Size 2) on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e (Size 4) has an Effective Size of 6. He can see over Size 5 walls that would blind him at \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP: HIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e is a powerhouse on the battlefield. When a Unit is on terrain with a Size of 3 or 4, the Effective Size of that Unit goes through the roof, letting it peer over barriers that would block the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e of Units on lower ground. The best position for ranged support is to utilise HIGH GROUND, as you can rain down fire from above. The downside, of course, is that Units on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e are exposed to just about everything, so only put Units there if they can handle whatever is coming their way. Ranged specialists with good Armour or Evade stats are the ones that really shine from \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e, but Units with lower stats should remain on the ground if they want to stay hidden.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eTop-Down Perspective:\u003c/b\u003e Only terrain pieces that rise vertically between the two models' positions (as viewed from above) can block the shot. The horizontal surface a model stands on does not obstruct the top-down trace.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eStacking Terrain: \u003c/b\u003eWhen a terrain piece is set on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e or \u003cb\u003eMID GROUND\u003c/b\u003e, its Effective Size increases in the same way as a model’s - it gains the Size of the terrain it stands on.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example, \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003ea Marauder (Size 2) is on \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e (Size 3), giving it an Effective Size of 5. A ruined wall (Size 2) is also on \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e (Size 3), giving it an Effective Size of 5. Because they have the same Effective Size, the Marauder cannot see over the ruined wall. The Roach (Size 2) at \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e cannot make a \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e with the Marauder because the ruined wall (Effective Size 5) blocks it.                                               "stringValue": "\u003cb\u003eMarkers \u003c/b\u003eare used to keep track of status or game states. Unlike Tokens, they have no physical presence. They do not block \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e or Movement.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eMission Markers \u003c/b\u003eare numbered Markers used on the battlefield during Setup at coordinates shown on the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e. Each Marker is 32mm in diameter and has two sides:\u003cb\u003e Activated\u003c/b\u003e or \u003cb\u003eDeactivated\u003c/b\u003e. Each one is colour-coded by number: Markers 1 & 3 are Red, Markers 2 & 4 are Blue, and Marker 5 is Neutral.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eActivation Markers \u003c/b\u003eare set beside the Unit that has completed its turn in a Phase. They are double-sided with the arrow facing upwards, showing that the Unit has finished its turn in Phase 1 (Movement). The reverse side indicates that the Unit has completed its turn in Phase 2 (Assault).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eFaction Indicators \u003c/b\u003eare used on \u003cb\u003eMission Markers\u003c/b\u003e to show which player controls that Mission Marker at any moment. Some \u003cb\u003eSpecial Abilities\u003c/b\u003e utilise Faction Indicators to mark an area of the battlefield.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eZone of Influence Markers\u003c/b\u003e are used to define the \u003cb\u003eZone of Influence\u003c/b\u003e when the \u003cb\u003eEntry Edge\u003c/b\u003e doesn’t extend along the entire table edge. These are L-shaped corner markers that must be set exactly as shown on the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eFirst Player Marker \u003c/b\u003eis used to track which player has initiative. The holder chooses which player activates first at the beginning of each Phase. The Marker passes between players throughout the game, usually when a player Passes early in a Phase or when Victory Points are tallied at the end of the Round."

Bring them onto the battlefield during the Movement Phase as Supply allows.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE: \u003c/b\u003eStarting each Unit in Reserve is a deliberate departure from traditional miniature wargaming. Instead of deploying the whole army on the table at the start and committing to those positions before rolling a single die, players develop their battlefield presence gradually through each Round. This approach is similar to how a traditional real-time strategy game develops its economic presence – early Rounds require decisions on which Units to commit with limited Supply, while later Rounds punish those who didn’t manage these early decisions effectively. It also helps to eliminate the common problem of alpha-striking on Turn 1."

Grass does not block movement but does block \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight,\u003c/b\u003e following the standard Cover rules (Part 7.1.1). If the \u003cb\u003eLeading Model\u003c/b\u003e’s path of travel passes through or any model of a Unit ends on a Grass terrain piece, that Grass piece is immediately removed from the game for the remainder of the battle.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eFlying Units: \u003c/b\u003eA \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit moving over Grass does not destroy the Grass terrain piece. \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003emodels pass above the terrain, not through it. If any model of a Flying Unit ends on a Grass terrain piece, it is removed as normal.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eSize 2 and larger:\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003eCannot\u003c/b\u003e move through.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eELEVATION\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eModels can stand one of three elevations:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL:\u003c/b\u003e Standing directly on the playmat.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eMID GROUND:\u003c/b\u003e Standing on horizontal terrain of Size 1 or 2.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND:\u003c/b\u003e Standing on horizontal terrain of Size 3 or larger.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eThe model stands on Elevation if its entire base is at that elevation. If the model’s base is on multiple elevation levels, assume it is standing on the lowest of those elevations.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eACCESS POINTS\u003c/b\u003e connect different elevation levels. Models change elevation only by moving through an \u003cb\u003eACCESS POINT\u003c/b\u003e (examples: ladders, portals, doors).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eRAMPS\u003c/b\u003e are Size 1 \u003cb\u003eMID GROUND\u003c/b\u003e terrain. A model on a ramp at any point along its surface is at \u003cb\u003eMID GROUND\u003c/b\u003e elevation. Models cannot pass through a ramp freely - they may only enter and exit through the ramp’s two \u003cb\u003eACCESS POINTS\u003c/b\u003e (one at the base, one at the top) and may end their movement on the ramp.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003c VISUAL: Marine moving from GROUND LEVEL through ACCESS POINT to RAMP, then through second ACCESS POINT to HIGH GROUND \u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFLYING MOVE\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eUnits with the \u003cb\u003eFlying Combat Tag\u003c/b\u003e ignore all normal movement restrictions.                                               "stringValue": "Fire is the language of the Assault Phase. A volley of Gauss Rifle rounds tears through a Unit caught crossing open ground. A Hydralisk spine salvo pins down an advancing squad behind a wall. A single Siege Tank shell lands among a cluster of infantry and scatters them. Every ranged weapon on the battlefield has the potential to reshape the fight before the enemy can close the distance, but only if the shot is aimed at the right target, at the right time, with the right weapon.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA Ranged Attack is resolved in two stages. First, the attacking player selects a valid target and assigns weapons to it. Second, the attack is resolved through the three-pool system: dice move from the Attack Pool through the Armour Pool to the Damage Pool, with each stage giving both sides a chance to influence the outcome. Units with multiple weapon profiles may split their fire across different targets, resolving each weapon as a separate Batch.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e1. TARGET ELIGIBILITY\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA valid target \u003cb\u003emust\u003c/b\u003e meet all of the following criteria:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eVisible \u003c/b\u003emodels from the target Unit are \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e the weapon’s maximum \u003cb\u003eRange\u003c/b\u003e. Measure from the attacking model’s base to the target model’s base.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Only models \u003cb\u003eWithin \u003c/b\u003eRange and Visible contribute dice to the Attack Roll.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The target’s \u003cb\u003eCombat Tag\u003c/b\u003e matches the weapon’s target characteristic (\u003cb\u003eGround\u003c/b\u003e, \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eor \u003cb\u003eAll\u003c/b\u003e).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eEngagement Status:\u003c/b\u003e An \u003cb\u003eUnengaged\u003c/b\u003e attacking Unit cannot select an \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e Unit as a target (except Spillover from Template Weapons - see Part 8.7.6). An \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e attacking Unit may only target the Unit(s) it is currently \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e with.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e2. WEAPON SELECTION AND BATCHING\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEach model fires one of its available Assault Phase weapons. All models using the same \u003cb\u003eWeapon Profile \u003c/b\u003emust fire at the same target - the player cannot split a single profile’s fire. A Batch consists of all models firing the same weapon at the same target. This same-profile, same-target rule applies to \u003cb\u003eSIDEARM\u003c/b\u003e weapons as well - all models firing the same \u003cb\u003eSIDEARM\u003c/b\u003e profile must target the same Unit, although that Unit may differ from the target of the Unit’s other weapons.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eREMOVING DICE: \u003c/b\u003eWhen a \u003cb\u003eSpecial Ability\u003c/b\u003e reduces the number of dice within a Batch, the player controlling the Unit resolving that ability chooses which dice are removed.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP:\u003c/b\u003e Batch sequencing provides a slight advantage. By declaring and resolving each Batch individually, you can use the first Batch to weaken or eliminate your target, then modify the second Batch depending on the result. If your Unit has two weapon profiles, use the one more likely to eliminate your \u003cb\u003eDamaged Enemy \u003c/b\u003efirst. If that works out, your second profile can be used to engage a new enemy. Remember that if your models have the same weapon, they must fire at the same target. When building your army, Units with single powerful weapon profiles are more \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e-focused but less flexible, while Units with multiple profile \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eare more flexible with multiple targets.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf a Unit has multiple Weapon Profiles, it may fire at different targets - resolved in separate Batches.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eBATCH SEQUENCE: \u003c/b\u003eDeclare the target of one Batch, resolve it fully, and then declare the next Batch. The player does not declare all targets simultaneously.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE:\u003c/b\u003e If a Batch Destroys the \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003eUnit your \u003cb\u003eFriendly \u003c/b\u003eUnit was \u003cb\u003eEngaged \u003c/b\u003ewith, that \u003cb\u003eFriendly \u003c/b\u003eUnit immediately becomes \u003cb\u003eUnengaged\u003c/b\u003e (unless still \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e with another enemy). Remaining Batches may target freely."

                                              "stringValue": "Every attack is resolved by moving dice through three pools. Dice begin in the Attack Pool, pass through the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e, and end in the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e. Dice that survive the entire sequence inflict casualties.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAttack Pool.\u003c/b\u003e Generate a number of dice equal to each attacking model’s \u003cb\u003eRate of Attack (RoA)\u003c/b\u003e. Roll all dice in this pool against the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eHit\u003c/b\u003e characteristic. Each die that meets or exceeds the \u003cb\u003eHit\u003c/b\u003e value is a success. Move it to the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e. Discard all failures.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eArmour Pool.\u003c/b\u003e The defender rolls all dice in this pool against the target Unit’s \u003cb\u003eArmour\u003c/b\u003e characteristic. Each die that meets or exceeds the \u003cb\u003eArmour\u003c/b\u003e value is a success. Discard it. Move all failures to the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e. Some effects bypass this roll entirely: dice moved out of the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool \u003c/b\u003eby Surge or \u003cb\u003eCRITICAL HIT\u003c/b\u003e are set directly into the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool \u003c/b\u003ewithout an\u003cb\u003e Armour Roll\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDamage Pool.\u003c/b\u003e Each die remaining in this pool inflicts \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eequal to the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e characteristic. If the target Unit is eligible for an \u003cb\u003eEvade Roll\u003c/b\u003e, the defender rolls all dice in this pool against the Unit’s \u003cb\u003eEvade\u003c/b\u003e characteristic before \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eis applied. Each die that meets or exceeds the \u003cb\u003eEvade\u003c/b\u003e value is a success and is discarded. Remaining dice inflict \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eas normal.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eResolve each Batch in sequence:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e1. ROLL TO HIT\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• For each attacking model with an eligible target, add dice equal to the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eRoA\u003c/b\u003e to the Attack Pool.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• If the weapon has an \u003cb\u003eS Dice\u003c/b\u003e characteristic, add one \u003cb\u003eSurge Die \u003c/b\u003e(use a different colour). If there is no S Dice, the Surge Result is 0.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Roll all Attack Dice. Results equal to or higher than the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eHit\u003c/b\u003e value are successes. Move successful dice to the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE:\u003c/b\u003e If dice in the same Batch have different modifiers, roll them separately. It still counts as the same Batch.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e2. RESOLVE SURGE\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Check if the target Unit’s \u003cb\u003eCombat Tag\u003c/b\u003e matches the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eSurge Type\u003c/b\u003e. If not, the \u003cb\u003eSurge Die \u003c/b\u003eresult is ignored entirely - discard it. No dice move from the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e at this step.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• If it matches, move a number of dice equal to the \u003cb\u003eSurge Die result\u003c/b\u003e from the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e directly to the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e. These bypass \u003cb\u003eArmour \u003c/b\u003eentirely. Surge can \u003cb\u003enever\u003c/b\u003e move more dice than are currently in the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP: \u003c/b\u003eSurge stands out as one of the most efficient sources of \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003ebecause \u003cb\u003eSurge Dice \u003c/b\u003ebypasses the entire Armour rolling process. Before firing off any Rounds, always check that the \u003cb\u003eSurge Type \u003c/b\u003eof your chosen weapon aligns with the target’s Combat Tag. Using Anti-\u003cb\u003eGround\u003c/b\u003e Surge on a \u003cb\u003eGround\u003c/b\u003e target can double or triple your \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eoutput compared to firing at a \u003cb\u003eFlying\u003c/b\u003e target with the same weapon. When building your army, be sure to select weapons with \u003cb\u003eSurge Types \u003c/b\u003ethat match the Combat Tags you are most likely to encounter.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e3. ARMOUR ROLLS\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The defender rolls all dice in the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Results equal to or higher than the Unit’s \u003cb\u003eArmour\u003c/b\u003e characteristic: \u003cb\u003esuccess\u003c/b\u003e - discard the die.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Results lower than Armour: \u003cb\u003efailure\u003c/b\u003e - move the die to the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e4. EVADE ROLLS\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003ePerform this step only if the target Unit qualifies:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eSpecial Ability \u003c/b\u003eor keyword grants an \u003cb\u003eEvade Roll\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The target is \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e and is suffering \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003efrom a \u003cb\u003eRanged Attack\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf eligible, the defender rolls all dice in the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e. Results equal to or higher than the Unit’s \u003cb\u003eEvade\u003c/b\u003e characteristic: \u003cb\u003esuccess\u003c/b\u003e - remove those dice. Remaining dice are confirmed \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e5. RESOLVE DAMAGE AND CASUALTIES\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Multiply the remaining dice in the \u003cb\u003eDamage Pool\u003c/b\u003e by the weapon’s \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e characteristic.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Add any previously accumulated \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003e(from earlier attacks in this or previous Rounds), indicated by a \u003cb\u003eDamage Marker\u003c/b\u003e. This total is the \u003cb\u003eTotal Damage\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Apply any Special Skills that reduce the Total \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Remove casualties model by model. The defending player removes models from the target Unit, following these rules:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The attack \u003cb\u003ecannot\u003c/b\u003e remove more models than the number of \u003cb\u003eVisible\u003c/b\u003e models in the target Unit.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• While Total \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eequals or exceeds a model’s HP, remove one Visible model and reduce Total \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eby that model’s HP. Repeat.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• If all Visible models are Destroyed, discard remaining Total \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003e- it does not carry over to non-Visible models.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• If Total \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003eremains but \u003cb\u003ecannot\u003c/b\u003e Destroy the next Visible model, record it with a \u003cb\u003eDamage Marker\u003c/b\u003e (e.g. a D6 set next to the Unit)."

Once only one valid casualty remains, the controlling player may choose either the last A or B.\u003c/i\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE:\u003c/b\u003e The \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e casualty priority system prevents the defending player from picking off models to escape Engagements they would rather not be in. Otherwise, an opponent could absorb \u003cb\u003eDamage \u003c/b\u003efrom shooting by taking the single model that is holding them in a difficult melee combat, effectively giving their \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003ea free \u003cb\u003eDisengage\u003c/b\u003e action. The priority makes shooting at a melee force eat away at the outer models first, protecting the core of the melee until the \u003cb\u003eEngaged\u003c/b\u003e models are removed."

                                              "stringValue": "\u003cb\u003eBLAST TEMPLATE (BT) / FLAMER TEMPLATE (FT)\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e1. ALIGNMENT\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eBT:\u003c/b\u003e The centre hole \u003cb\u003emust\u003c/b\u003e sit over the target model’s base (\u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e if possible). The position of the centre hole is the \u003cb\u003eTarget Point\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eFT:\u003c/b\u003e The narrow end must be flush with the attacking model’s base edge and aimed at the target. The centre of the target model’s base is the \u003cb\u003eTarget Point\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Templates affect only models at the \u003cb\u003esame elevation level\u003c/b\u003e as the \u003cb\u003eTarget Point\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003emodels are not on any elevation level for template purposes. A template set at \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e does not affect \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003emodels, and a template cannot be set on a \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003emodel’s elevation level, unless the template weapon has Target: ALL or Target: \u003cb\u003eFlying\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP: \u003c/b\u003eTemplate weapons need careful placement. A well-timed Blast Template can hit two or three Units at once, causing spillover Batches in addition to the main \u003cb\u003eDamage\u003c/b\u003e. Pay attention to turns when the \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003ehas a \"bunch\" of Units around the same terrain piece or \u003cb\u003eMission Marker\u003c/b\u003e. Flamer Templates have a shorter range but almost always hit everything \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e the cone, making them very effective against tightly packed melee Units. When facing armies that heavily rely on Templates, keep your Units at maximum \u003cb\u003eCoherency\u003c/b\u003e and avoid having too many Units on a single objective.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e2. DECLARING TARGETS\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eFollow standard Target Eligibility (Part 8.7.3) with this exception: select one \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003eUnit as the Primary target - all models in that Unit covered by the template are the Main target. Every other model (\u003cb\u003eFriendly \u003c/b\u003eor \u003cb\u003eEnemy\u003c/b\u003e) covered by the template is resolved under \u003cb\u003eSpillover\u003c/b\u003e, provided they share the same elevation and Combat Tag as the Primary target.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e3. DETERMINING HITS\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA model is affected if all of the following are true:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Its base is partially or fully covered by the template.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• It is on the same elevation as the declared \u003cb\u003eTarget Point\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A line traced from the \u003cb\u003eCentre Hole\u003c/b\u003e (BT) or \u003cb\u003eAttacking Model’s base\u003c/b\u003e (FT) to the model’s base is not blocked by terrain piece (Size 2+).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• It is an eligible target type (e.g., a \u003cb\u003eGround\u003c/b\u003e-only template does not affect \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003emodels, even if it is covered).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e4. ATTACK POOL GENERATION\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eMain Target:\u003c/b\u003e Generate a number of Attack Dice equal to the number of Affected models in the target Unit, plus any weapon Rate of Attack modifiers.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eSpillover (separate Batches per Unit):\u003c/b\u003e Generate a number of Attack Dice equal to the number of Affected models in that Unit only. Do not apply Rate of Attack modifiers. Do not apply Surge.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e5. RESOLUTION\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Roll to Hit as normal. Roll the generated Attack Dice for the Batch. Any result equal to or higher than the weapon’s Hit characteristic is a success and is moved to the \u003cb\u003eArmour Pool\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Do not roll a \u003cb\u003eSurge Die\u003c/b\u003e. For the Main target, the Surge Result equals the number of Affected models in that Unit. During the Combat Phase, \u003cb\u003eEngaged \u003c/b\u003eUnits close the distance to their foes and trade blows in brutal melee combat. Unlike the previous Phases, where activation is voluntary, every Unit currently in the \u003cb\u003eEngagement Range\u003c/b\u003e of an \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003emust act in this Phase. Hence, placing a high-Supply Unit on the objective can sometimes be a better strategy than scattering weakened Units across it. On the other hand, if your foe is holding a Marker with a single strong Unit, you must have the combined Supply to win the battle, not simply the numbers. It is also worth noting that a Unit at Supply 0 will still hold the Marker if no one contests it, so a weakened Unit is not necessarily useless.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eCALCULATE CONTROL\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eFor each Marker:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Each player sums the \u003cb\u003eCurrent Supply Value\u003c/b\u003e of all their contesting Units.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The player with the \u003cb\u003ehigher\u003c/b\u003e total \u003cb\u003eControls\u003c/b\u003e the Marker.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003etie\u003c/b\u003e means the Marker is \u003cb\u003eContested\u003c/b\u003e - control does not change.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A Unit at Supply 0 may still Control a Marker if no \u003cb\u003eEnemy \u003c/b\u003eUnits contest it.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eSTICKY CONTROL\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eSet a \u003cb\u003eFaction Indicator\u003c/b\u003e on each controlled Marker. Once a Marker is controlled, it remains under that player’s control - even if they move Units away - until the opponent actively reclaims it by ending a Scoring Phase with a higher contesting Supply total. A \u003cb\u003eContested\u003c/b\u003e result (tied Supply) \u003cb\u003enever\u003c/b\u003e transfers control: the Marker stays with whoever currently holds it, or remains neutral if it has never been controlled. A Marker \u003cb\u003ecannot\u003c/b\u003e become neutral again once a player has taken control of it.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE:\u003c/b\u003e Sticky Control means that a location becomes yours until the opponent re-takes it from you. This prevents the irritating problem in some wargames where you grab a location, push forward to grab another, and the first location reverts to no one in particular. It encourages bold play, taking what you want and holding it, and moving forward to take more. It creates a real strategic challenge, too, because taking a Marker forces the opponent to use real resources to take the objective rather than just waiting for you to leave."
                                            }
                                          }
                                        }
                                      }
                                    ]
                                  }

The winner takes the \u003cb\u003eFirst Player Marker\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Begin Phase 1 of the next Round.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDESIGNER’S NOTE: \u003c/b\u003eThe choice of initiative going to the player with fewer Victory Points is a \"catch-up\" mechanic. The player behind goes first in the next Round, giving them a chance to reposition and compete for objectives before the leading player can secure their position. This prevents a runaway lead where the player who starts ahead always remains ahead by an ever-widening gap. When the Passing mechanic is included (where the first player to \u003cb\u003ePass\u003c/b\u003e gets the \u003cb\u003eFirst Player Marker\u003c/b\u003e for the next Phase), initiative is no longer a static advantage but a fluid resource."

It does not matter how a miniature is posed, whether a Zealot is mid-leap or a Hydralisk is rearing back to strike; the rules see only the base. Every measurement, every \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e check, and every question about whether two models are touching or overlapping is resolved by looking at their bases, nothing else.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEvery model must be mounted on the correct base size as specified on its \u003cb\u003eUnit Card\u003c/b\u003e. Using the wrong base size changes a model’s physical footprint and directly affects gameplay, so consistency matters.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eNo Overlap: \u003c/b\u003eBases may never overlap. If a model cannot be set without its base overlapping another base or impassable terrain, it simply cannot go there.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eScenic Freedom: \u003c/b\u003ePlayers are free to add scenic basing, custom conversions, player dramatic poses, and flight stands. The game encourages creativity - just know that, for rules purposes, the base and the Size Characteristic on the \u003cb\u003eUnit Card\u003c/b\u003e are the only things that count. A Marine standing on a pile of rubble is no taller than one standing on a bare base. A Mutalisk on a towering flight stand has the same Size as one on a short peg. \u003cb\u003eFlight Stands:\u003c/b\u003e If a model uses a flight stand, the bottom of the stand counts as the model's base for all measurements and positioning.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eWobbly Model Syndrome\u003c/b\u003e: When a model cannot sit flat on the terrain, both players should agree on where the model would stand if the surface allowed it. Set the model as close to that spot as possible, or use a marker to indicate its actual position. The model is treated as occupying the agreed position for all purposes."

                                  "stringValue": "At any given moment, each player occupies one or more of the following roles. These terms appear throughout the rules and determine who makes decisions, who rolls dice, and who is affected by an ability.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eActive Player:\u003c/b\u003e The player whose turn it is to act. Some rules, particularly \u003cb\u003eReactions\u003c/b\u003e, refer to this to determine priority when both sides respond to the same event.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eControlling Player: \u003c/b\u003eThe player who commands a specific Unit, model, or Token. They make all decisions and roll all dice. Assume that \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnits’ \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e is higher than the \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of any terrain piece on the table.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit does not benefit from \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e Cover (Part 7.1.3).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit cannot Control or Contest \u003cb\u003eMission Markers \u003c/b\u003e(overrides Parts 6.2 and 8.9.1).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit cannot \u003cb\u003eCharge \u003c/b\u003eor be \u003cb\u003eCharged\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit cannot participate in the Combat Phase (Part 8.8).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• A \u003cb\u003eFlying \u003c/b\u003eUnit ignores elevation. It does not use \u003cb\u003eAccess Points\u003c/b\u003e. For Cover and \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight \u003c/b\u003epurposes, treat a \u003cb\u003eFlying\u003c/b\u003e unit's \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e as higher than the Effective Size of any terrain piece on the table (Part 7.1.4). In the final Round of the game, the \u003cb\u003eSupply Pool\u003c/b\u003e becomes unlimited and \u003cb\u003eAvailable Supply\u003c/b\u003e restrictions are lifted."
                                            }
                                          }
                                        }
                                      }
                                    ]

                                              "stringValue": "\u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e determines what a model can see and, by extension, what it can target with attacks and abilities.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eAll \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e checks are resolved from a \u003cb\u003e2D top-down perspective\u003c/b\u003e, looking directly down at the battlefield from above. To check whether a model can see a target, trace an imaginary straight line from \u003cb\u003eany part\u003c/b\u003e of the acting model's base to \u003cb\u003eany part\u003c/b\u003e of the target model's base. Vertical height is never factored into the trace.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf the trace does not pass through any \u003cb\u003eBlocking Terrain\u003c/b\u003e (any terrain piece with an \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of 1 or greater), the target is \u003cb\u003eVisible\u003c/b\u003e. No further checks are required.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eIf the trace passes through \u003cb\u003eBlocking Terrain\u003c/b\u003e, the target is not automatically hidden. Apply the Cover rules (Part 7.1.1) to determine whether that terrain actually blocks the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eFull Cover:\u003c/b\u003e The terrain's \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e is equal to or greater than the \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of \u003cb\u003eboth\u003c/b\u003e the attacker and the target. \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is blocked.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eDirect Cover:\u003c/b\u003e The trace passes through a terrain piece, and either the attacker or the target is \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of that terrain, provided the terrain's \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e is equal to or greater than the \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of the model that is \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e. \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is blocked. \u003cb\u003eException:\u003c/b\u003e If both the attacker and the target are \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the same terrain piece and \u003cb\u003eWithin 3\"\u003c/b\u003e of each other, resolve \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e normally.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eElevation Dead Zone:\u003c/b\u003e A model on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e (Size 3+) cannot see a model at \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e that is \u003cb\u003eWithin 1\"\u003c/b\u003e of the base of the same terrain piece, and vice versa. The same Close Quarters exception applies.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEach terrain piece is assessed independently. Terrain pieces do not combine their \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e or proximity. If no single terrain piece meets the requirements for Full Cover or Direct Cover, \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is not blocked regardless of how many terrain pieces the trace passes through.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA terrain piece's footprint is defined by its physical base or outermost edges viewed from above. Gaps, windows, doorways, and open interiors within the footprint \u003cb\u003edo block\u003c/b\u003e the \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e unless players agree otherwise during Battlefield Setup (Part 7.1).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFlying\u003c/b\u003e models ignore the Full Cover rule. Direct Cover and the Elevation Dead Zone still apply. Treat a \u003cb\u003eFlying\u003c/b\u003e model's \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e as higher than the \u003cb\u003eEffective Size\u003c/b\u003e of any terrain piece on the table (Part 7.1.4).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e is reciprocal: if Model A can see Model B, Model B can see Model A through the same trace."

There are no restrictions on pre-measuring. Players are encouraged to measure thoroughly and agree on distances before committing to an action.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eBetween Models:\u003c/b\u003e Measure from the nearest point of one model's base to the nearest point of the other model's base. For models on flight stands, the bottom of the stand is treated as the model's base for all measurements (Part 2.3).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eIgnore Overhang:\u003c/b\u003e Weapons, wings, limbs, and scenic elements extending beyond the base rim are ignored.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eBase-to-Base Contact:\u003c/b\u003e If two bases are physically touching, the distance between them is \u003cb\u003e0\"\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eTokens and Markers:\u003c/b\u003e Measure to the nearest physical edge.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eElevation:\u003c/b\u003e When calculating distances between models at different elevations, always measure horizontally from a top-down perspective. The vertical height difference should not be included in your measurements. This applies to Range, \u003cb\u003eEngagement Range\u003c/b\u003e, and the ranges of abilities. Movement distances are measured as specified by the action being performed (see Part 8.5.3).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003c VISUAL: Three examples - flat ground measurement, measuring around terrain, measuring to a model on elevation \u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example,\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e the \u003c/i\u003edistance between models is measured from the closest point of one model’s base to the closest point of the other model’s base.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example,\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e the \u003c/i\u003edistance between a model and a terrain piece is measured from the closest point of the model’s base to the closest edge of the terrain piece.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example, \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003ethe distance measurement from Marine on \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e to a Marine at \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e is measured horizontally from a direct overhead view, ignoring the vertical height of the terrain."

                                "value": {
                                  "stringValue": "\u003cb\u003eWITHIN\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA model is \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e a distance if any part of its base touches or crosses into that range. A Unit is \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e a distance if at least one model’s base touches or crosses into that range.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eWHOLLY WITHIN\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA model is \u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e a distance only if its entire base sits inside that range - no part of the base may extend beyond the edge. A Unit is \u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e only if every model’s base in the Unit satisfies this condition.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA5 example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example,\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e \u003c/i\u003ea Marine measures 3\" from its base. Zergling A is \u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e this 3\" range - its entire base sits inside it. Zergling B is \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e 3\" of the Marine - part of its base touches the range, but not all of it. Zergling C is outside the 3\" range entirely. The Zergling Unit is considered to be \u003cb\u003eWithin\u003c/b\u003e 3\" of the Marine because at least one model (Zergling A) is in range. However, the Zergling Unit is not \u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e 3\" since models B and C are not \u003cb\u003eWholly Within\u003c/b\u003e this range.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eMaly side EXAMPLE 2.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003c\u003cA6 SIDE example\u003e\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eIn this example, \u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003ea Unit of Raptors with all of its models \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eWholly Within\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e 3\" of its \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eLeading Model\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e that is on \u003c/i\u003e\u003cb\u003e\u003ci\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/i\u003e\u003c/b\u003e\u003ci\u003e. The distance is measured horizontally as viewed from directly above - the vertical height of the terrain is ignored.\u003c/i\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDesigner’s Note: \u003c/b\u003eSome Units have special rules that allow their models to occupy different elevations. Clearance governs movement through a space, not stopping inside one.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eOpenings in terrain pieces - such as archways, doorways, and breaches - are treated as gaps for the purpose of Gap Clearance, even if the surrounding terrain piece is Size 2 or larger. The gap must be wide enough for the model’s Size category.                                             "value": {
                                              "stringValue": "The player chooses one of the three races - \u003cb\u003eTerran\u003c/b\u003e, \u003cb\u003eZerg\u003c/b\u003e, or \u003cb\u003eProtoss\u003c/b\u003e, and then selects a single \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e. This card forms the basis of the army, providing the initial organisation slots (e.g., \u003cb\u003eKerrigan’s Swarm\u003c/b\u003e 3× Core, 1× Hero, 2× Support) and determining which Units and \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e may be included.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFaction Tag Eligibility\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEvery card in the game features \u003cb\u003eFaction Tags\u003c/b\u003e, which indicate the faction it belongs to. A \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e always displays a Race Tag (e.g., \u003cb\u003eZerg\u003c/b\u003e) and usually includes a \u003cb\u003eSub-Faction Tag \u003c/b\u003eas well (e.g., \u003cb\u003eKERRIGAN’S BROOD\u003c/b\u003e). \u003cb\u003eUnit Cards\u003c/b\u003e and \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e also carry their own \u003cb\u003eFaction Tags \u003c/b\u003ein the same manner.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eWhen building an army, the player checks whether a Unit or \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e is allowed by comparing its tags to the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e. The rule is simple: every tag on the Unit or \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e must also appear on the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e. If even one tag does not match, that card cannot be included in the army. It does not matter how many other tags match; a single incorrect tag is enough to disqualify it.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eCards with fewer tags than the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e are perfectly fine. A Unit only requires its own tags to be present; it does not need to match every tag the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e has.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eEXAMPLE:\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA player selects the \u003cb\u003eZerg Swarm\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e, which has one \u003cb\u003eFaction Tag\u003c/b\u003e: \u003cb\u003eZerg\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eZerglings \u003c/b\u003e(\u003cb\u003eFaction Tags\u003c/b\u003e: \u003cb\u003eZerg\u003c/b\u003e) - \u003cb\u003eEligible\u003c/b\u003e. Always check the Tournament Organiser’s rules pack before attending.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDefault: Open Lists\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eBy default, both players share their entire army rosters - including all Unit selections, upgrades, and weapon swaps with each other before the game starts. Since \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e and the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e are already set face-up on the table, Open Lists go one step further by revealing exactly which Units and upgrades the opponent has selected. This enables both players to plan their strategy with full information and is the recommended way to play.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eOptional: Closed Lists\u003c/b\u003e Before the game begins, both players may agree to play with Closed Lists instead. If either player does not agree, default to Open Lists.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eUnder Closed Lists, army rosters are hidden. Neither player is required to reveal their \u003cb\u003eArmy List\u003c/b\u003e or Unit upgrades before the game starts. The specific Units in a player’s roster are discovered during play as they are deployed. However, all \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e and the \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e must still be set face-up on the table before the game begins. Both players may inspect each other’s \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e and \u003cb\u003eFaction Cards\u003c/b\u003e at any time.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eOnce a Unit is set on the battlefield, the controlling player must immediately inform the opponent of any upgrades or weapon swaps that the Unit carries. This includes replacement weapons purchased through the Upgrade system (Part 9.1.7) or any other modifications that affect how the Unit behaves. The opponent is entitled to inspect the \u003cb\u003eUnit Card\u003c/b\u003e and any associated \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e at any time while that Unit is on the table.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP:\u003c/b\u003e While Open Lists are the default, we strongly recommend trying Closed Lists for the best StarCraft experience. The way Units are introduced to the battlefield one at a time mirrors the fog of war that defines StarCraft: you scout, you react, you adapt. Not knowing exactly what your opponent is fielding until it hits the table creates genuine tension and rewards sharp play. Before the first Unit ever hits the table, take a look at your opponent’s \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e and \u003cb\u003eFaction Card\u003c/b\u003e. Each \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e has its own set of \u003cb\u003eArmy Slots\u003c/b\u003e: Core, Elite, Support, Air, and Hero. These slots determine which Units can occupy them. By studying what’s on the table, an experienced player can make an educated guess about which Units are still viable in their opponent’s roster. The Barracks \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e suggests Marines and Marauders. The Spawning Pool \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e suggests Zerglings. The Robotics Facility \u003cb\u003eTactical Card\u003c/b\u003e suggests Colossi and Immortals. Reading your opponent’s \u003cb\u003eTactical Cards\u003c/b\u003e is your first act of scouting - just like in the video game."

                                "value": {
                                  "stringValue": "Before the game starts, players use a short draft to determine the Mission and Deployment for the battle. The draft ensures neither player enters with a pre-arranged advantage - both sides have equal say in what is played and where.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eWHAT YOU NEED\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eEach player brings 2 \u003cb\u003eMission Cards\u003c/b\u003e and 2 \u003cb\u003eDeployment Cards\u003c/b\u003e to the table. A player may not bring duplicate cards in their own set, although both players may independently bring the same cards as each other.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eArrange all cards face-up in two rows:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eRow 1:\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003eMission Cards\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eRow 2: Deployment Cards\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eSTEP 1 - ROLL-OFF\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eBoth players Roll-Off (Part 3.2). The winner makes two choices, in order:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eChoice 1 - Colour: \u003c/b\u003eDeclare yourself the Red Player or the Blue Player. This determines your \u003cb\u003eEntry Edge\u003c/b\u003e, \u003cb\u003eZone of Influence\u003c/b\u003e, and \u003cb\u003eMission Marker\u003c/b\u003e affinity for the entire game.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003eChoice 2 - Draft Control:\u003c/b\u003e Choose to control either the \u003cb\u003eMission Draft\u003c/b\u003e or the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Draft\u003c/b\u003e. Your opponent automatically controls the other.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP: \u003c/b\u003eControlling the \u003cb\u003eMission Draft\u003c/b\u003e secures the victory conditions that suit your army. Controlling the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Draft \u003c/b\u003eshapes the geometry of the battlefield - tight deployment zones favour melee armies; spread-out zones favour ranged ones.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eSTEP 2 - RESOLVE THE MISSION DRAFT\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The player without \u003cb\u003eMission Draft\u003c/b\u003e control removes any 2 \u003cb\u003eMission Cards\u003c/b\u003e from the table.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The player with \u003cb\u003eMission Draft\u003c/b\u003e control selects 1 of the 2 remaining cards. This becomes the Mission for the game. Discard the last card.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eSTEP 3 - RESOLVE THE DEPLOYMENT DRAFT\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eRepeat the same process for the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Cards\u003c/b\u003e:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The player without \u003cb\u003eDeployment Draft\u003c/b\u003e control removes any 2 \u003cb\u003eDeployment Cards\u003c/b\u003e from the table.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• The player with \u003cb\u003eDeployment Draft\u003c/b\u003e control selects 1 of the 2 remaining cards. This becomes the Deployment for the game. Discard the last card.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eSTEP 4 - MARKER AFFINITY\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eOnce both cards are chosen, assign \u003cb\u003eMission Markers’\u003c/b\u003e affinity according to the Marker number:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eMarker Affinity:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Markers 1 and 3 begin under the Red Player's control.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Markers 2 and 4 begin under the Blue Player's control.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Marker 5 begins Neutral.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eMarker affinity indicates which player's colour is printed on each Marker. It does not grant starting control.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eProceed to Battlefield Setup (Part 9.3)."

                                  "stringValue": "Once the draft is complete and both cards have been chosen, the battlefield is set up in the following order.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• First, confirm the table dimensions as specified on the selected \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Second, assign \u003cb\u003eEntry Edges\u003c/b\u003e to each player as indicated on the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Third, set \u003cb\u003eZone of Influence Markers\u003c/b\u003e at the corners of each player’s \u003cb\u003eEntry Edge\u003c/b\u003e where the \u003cb\u003eEntry Edge\u003c/b\u003e does not run the full length of a table edge, exactly as instructed by the \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Fourth, set \u003cb\u003eMission Markers\u003c/b\u003e at the coordinates listed on the selected \u003cb\u003eDeployment Card\u003c/b\u003e.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• Finally, set terrain by either selecting or rolling for one of the pre-made maps on the last pages of the rulebook, or starting with the Red Player, players alternate placing one terrain piece at a time based on the terrain density guide below.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eTerrain Density Guidelines\u003c/b\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003eA balanced battlefield requires enough terrain for tactical choices without restricting movement or blocking sight lines. The following guidelines apply to a \u003cb\u003eStandard (36\" x\u003c/b\u003e \u003cb\u003e54\")\u003c/b\u003e table and should be scaled proportionally for other sizes.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eRecommended Terrain Count:\u003c/b\u003e 8 to 12 pieces total, distributed as follows:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e0 to 2 pieces of Size 0 \u003c/b\u003e(scatter terrain).\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e2 to 4 pieces of Size 1\u003c/b\u003e (barricades, low walls, scatter crates). These provide Cover for infantry but do not block \u003cb\u003eLine of Sight\u003c/b\u003e for anything larger than Size 1 models.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e4 to 6 pieces of Size 2\u003c/b\u003e (ruins, bunkers, wrecked vehicles). These form the backbone of the table, blocking LoS for most standard Units and creating the fire lanes and chokepoints that define the game.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e(If available) 1 to 2 pieces of Size 3+.\u003c/b\u003e These create \u003cb\u003eHIGH GROUND\u003c/b\u003e positions and block LoS for almost everything. Too many of these make ranged combat nearly impossible; too few leave the table feeling flat.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e• \u003cb\u003e4 to 6 pieces of Grass (Size 2 special)\u003c/b\u003e. These do not block movement but provide a natural LoS cover for Units advancing across open ground.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eDistribution:\u003c/b\u003e Divide the table visually into four quarters. Each quarter should contain at least 2 significant pieces (Size 2 or larger). No quarter should be completely empty, and none should be so dense that Units cannot manoeuvre through it.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eThe Centre: \u003c/b\u003eThe area \u003cb\u003eWithin 6\"\u003c/b\u003e of the table centre should contain at least one significant terrain piece. An empty centre creates a kill zone that punishes whoever moves first and can stall the game. Conversely, a completely blocked centre forces all engagements to the flanks.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eFire Lanes: \u003c/b\u003eEnsure that at least 2 clear fire lanes of 6\" or wider exist, running roughly from one \u003cb\u003eEntry Edge\u003c/b\u003e towards the other. Without fire lanes, ranged Units have no role, and melee armies dominate unchecked.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAccess Points:\u003c/b\u003e Every piece of Size 3+ terrain that models can stand on should have at least one ACCESS POINT reachable from \u003cb\u003eGROUND LEVEL\u003c/b\u003e without passing through another Size 2+ terrain piece. Elevated positions that are unreachable waste table space.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003cb\u003eAbathur’s TIP: \u003c/b\u003eThe placement of terrain is the very first strategic move of the game, made before any miniature is set on the board. If you have a force that excels at ranged combat, position your tall blocking terrain pieces towards the centre to block fire lanes along the edges and direct melee armies into confined spaces. If your force is better at close-range combat, manipulate the terrain to create opportunities for sneaky movements unseen by ranged fire. Always consider the \u003cb\u003eMission Markers\u003c/b\u003e; placing terrain near a Marker makes it easier to hold with Cover, while leaving a Marker exposed likely benefits those with the most aggressive ranged fire."
